Jamison Brereton

174
Indra
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Another hymn bursting with AgastyaтАЩs tricks, here especially in the realm of daring syntax and deliberate omission of key words. The hymn celebrates IndraтАЩs great deeds, especially his victories over multiple named and unnamed opponents. Allusions to374 I.174
the Vr╠еtra myth and the release of the waters recur throughout the hymn (vss. 2, 3, 9), though the name Vr╠еtra is mentioned only once (vs. 2). The first verse urges Indra to тАЬguard the gods,тАЭ and he appears in that role as protector of Agni and his ritual activities (vs. 3) and enforcer of the norms of ─Аrya society, as embodied in the three principal ─Аdityas (vs. 6). Others who break the ─Аrya social contrastтАФthe impious, the godless, the speakers of scorn, and the breakers of alliances (vss. 2, 6, 7, 8)тАФalso fall victim to Indra as enforcer. Thus, though the tone is martial, the message is moral.
Two separate devices structure the hymn. On the one hand, the vocative indra (always to be read trisyllabically) appears in the first p─Бda of every verse immedi ately after the caesura. On the other hand, there is ring composition: the first and last (10) verses name Indra as тАЬgiver of victorious powerтАЭ and тАЬprotector of men,тАЭ while verse 2 has numerous echoes in verses 7тАУ9.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, are king; they who are gods (are subject) to you; therefore, scatterer (of foes), do you protect and cherish us men; you are the protector of the good, the possessor of wealth, the extricator of us (from sin); you are true, the invester (of all with your lustre) the giver of strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You are king, Indra: guard those who are gods and the superior men; protect us, lordly one.
You, as lord of settlements, are our surpassing benefactor, you the real possessor of goods and giver of victorious power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All the standard tr. (also, e.g., Schlerath, K├╢nigtum 143, Hale Asura- 70, Oberlies ReligRV II.177) construe the rel. cl. y├й ca dev─Б╠Б(с╕е) loosely (very loosely) with r─Б╠Бj─Б (e.g., Geldner тАЬDu, Indra, bist der K├╢nig ├╝ber alle G├╢tter,тАЭ which entails not only assuming that r─Б╠Бj─Б can govern such a clause, but also ignoring the ca). Within the same general interpr. framework Witzel Got┼Н do try to account for the ca: тАЬтАж der K├╢nig ├╝ber (alle), auch die die G├╢tter sind.тАЭ This can all be avoided by interpr. the rel. cl. as part of the familiar syntagm тАЬX and which Y,тАЭ but in an inverse version with the conjoined rel. cl. first (rather like the inverse V─Бyav Indra┼Ы ca construction with the ca constituent first ): y├й ca dev─Б╠Бс╕е, тАж nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn. Renou, fld by Klein (DGRV I.127), does interpret it as an тАЬX and which Y construction,тАЭ but supplies a gen. тАЬof mortalsтАЭ with r─Б╠Бj─Б: тАЬтАж le roi (des hommes) et de (ceux) qui (sont) les dieux.тАЭ This is unnec.

because r├бkс╣г─Б can govern the conjoined NP. It is accented because it opens the p─Бda.

Another intricate тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction is found in vs. 3 (by my interpr).

Witzel Got┼Н unaccountably take r├бkс╣г─Б absolutely and construe nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn with p─Бh├н, which is ungrammatical because p─Бh├н is accented; its object (asm─Б╠Бn) follows.

Griffith

THOU art the King of all the Gods, O Indra: protect the men, O Asura, preserve us.
Thou Lord of Heroes, Maghavan, our saver, art faithful, very rich, the victory-giver.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have humbled the people, suing for pardon when you have destroyed their seven new cities; you the irrproachable have dispersed the flowing waters; you have destroyed Vс╣Ыtra for the sake of the youthful Purukutsa.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You have humbled the people: dano vi┼Ыa indra mс╣Ыdhrav─Бcas = make liberal men soft-spoken, d─Бnamanaso manuс╣гy─Бn indra mс╣Ыduv─Бcaс╕е kuru; another interpretation, based on rurhi, current aceptation: you have made the subject (rain), soliciting ofrbearance, descend (in showers); when you have rent asunder the gliding, world-filling (clouds), then, irreproachable one, you did make the wates flow in channels, and did open the chief cloud for young Purukutsa

Jamison Brereton

You subdued the clans whose speech was scornful, Indra, when you split the seven autumnal strongholds, their shelter.
You set the flooding waters in motion, faultless one. You made Vr╠еtra subject to the youth Purukutsa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The derivation of the 2nd sg. verb d├бnaс╕е is unclear. Most (see EWA s.v. DAMI ) associate it one way or another with тИЪdam тАШtame, subdueтАЩ – beginning with S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs gloss adamayaс╕е. Oldenberg and Geldner suggest that there is a by-root dan beside dam; Renou (GLV 81) concurs that it belongs to a тАЬfausse racine,тАЭ probably generated from athematic forms where the root-final would have been followed by an ending beginning with a dental (type 2nd-3rd sg. ├бgan to тИЪgam). Bloomfield (153) suggests itтАЩs a nonce blending of тИЪdam and тИЪhan. I wonder if it is not the detritus of the expected 9th cl. pres. *damn─Б╠Бti, which would be cognate with nasal presents elsewhere in Indo-European and is the stem underlying attested dam─Бy├б- (тЖР *d(a)mn-H-y├й/├│-) and damanya-. In our 2nd sg. injunc., expected *damn─Б╠Бs, the interior nasal cluster could have been simplified and the whole remodeled as a thematic form (unfortunately requiring also accent retraction). In fact, *damn─Б╠Бti might not be the expected form; a reconstructed *dm-ne-H-ti without restoration of a full-grade root syllable should yield *dan─Б╠Бti, which would have lost its obvious root connection with тИЪdam and could without too much difficulty be remodeled to the thematic stem we appear to have. The 9th class ramс╣З─Б╠Бti would have pursued a different remodeling path.

In a n. Witzel Got┼Н suggest an unlikely deriv. from тИЪd─Б тАШdivideтАЩ, with an *-├йnonominal suffix, hence тАЬDer ist Abtrenner des nachl├дssig redenden Stammes,тАЭ taking the nominals as gen. sg. rather than acc. pl. (as is grammatically possible). The only advantage I see to this is that it works better with the ostensible 3rd sg. d├бrt in b, but there are other ways to handle that form.

As was just noted, the verb of b, p─Бda-final dart (тИЪdс╣Ы), appears to be a 3rd sg., in an otherwise 2nd sg. vs. It also ends in a (more or less) illicit cluster (-rt, with nonradical -t). With Oldenberg I assume that the original form was *daс╕е (тЖР *dar тЖР*dar-s). A final -t was falsely restored, possibly redactionally, on the basis of the identical p─Бda in VI.20.10c, where the 3rd sg. is appropriate and the sandhi situation favors the retention of the -t.

Note the phonetic play in #rс╣З╠е ├│r … ├бrс╣З─Б(с╕е)#.

Purukutsa is chronologically out of place here. Elsewhere he is a semihistorical figure, the father of Trasadasyu and a contemporary of Sud─Бs, so Vrtra ╠е should be out of his league and his time period. But he does figure in VI.20.10, immediately after the p─Бda identical to our b: VI.20.10d h├бn d─Б╠Бs─лс╕е puruk├║ts─Бya ┼Ыikс╣гan тАЬHe [=Indra] smote the D─Бsa (clans), doing his best for Purukutsa,тАЭ where the action described can be contemporary (or in the immediate past) and therefore chronologically possible. I think it likely that Purukutsa has been imported from VI.20.10 to anticipate the more properly mythological Kutsa in vs. 5. These two agreements with VI.20.10 support each other and are good evidence for the dependence of our vs. on that vs. _________ 03
Geldner suggests that the ┼Ы┼л╠Бra- in ┼Ы┼л╠Бrapatn─лс╕е тАШwhose lord is a championтАЩ is Indra himself, which seems correct.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes vс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е тАж dy─Б╠Бс╣Г ca as the conjoined obj. of ├бj─Б тАШdriveтАЩ; the two objects are then picked up by y├йbhiс╕е (Geldner: тАЬF├╝hre die Heere тАж und den Himmel, mit denen тАжтАЭ). The problem (besides the question of whether itтАЩs possible or desirable to drive heaven anywhere) is that vс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е is fem. pl. and dy─Б╠Бm is masc. sg., and y├йbhiс╕е is neither one. I follow OldenbergтАЩs interpr., also adopted by Renou, that sees an тАЬX and which YтАЭ constr. – with the twist that the ca does not follow the rel. prn. (as in y├й ca dev─Б╠Бс╕е in 1a), but precedes it, with another part of the rel. cl. fronted around it (dy─Б╠Бс╣Г ca y├йbhiс╕е).

By either interpr. the rel. cl. lacks a verb. Oldenberg, Renou, and I supply тАШgain, conquerтАЩ with heaven as obj. (And in keeping with the constant theme of these Agastya hymns, I assume the referent of y├йbhiс╕е is the Maruts; Oldenberg simply тАЬdie LeuteтАЭ; Renou doesnтАЩt specify.) Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] тАЬverb├╝ndet bist,тАЭ which seems kind of lame.

Initial r├бkс╣гo in c is Pragс╣Ыhya in the Pp., presumably 2nd sg. impv. r├бkс╣гa + u.

The standard tr. take a┼Ы├║с╣гaс╣Г t┼л╠Бrvay─Бnam as two PNs, but I see no reason to.

As noted in the comm. ad I.101.2, a┼Ы├║с╣гa- is otherwise only used of the demon ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, but this strong association surely results from their phonetic similarity. Semantically it fits Agni quite well. As for t┼л╠Бrvay─Бna- it is sometimes a PN (e.g., I.53.10), but its first member must be based on the verb stem t┼л╠Бrvati тАШgo in triumphтАЩ vel sim., and the literal sense of the compound is appropriate for Agni. See the very similar analytic phrase VI.15.5 t┼л╠Бrvan n├б y─Б╠Бman тАЬlike the one going in triumph on his course,тАЭ where Agni is the referent.

There is difference of opinion on how the simile works in d. Flg. Oldenberg, Renou, and the line of least resistance, I resupply the verb r├бkс╣гa from c, maintaining Indra as subj., compared to a lion. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take the subj. as Agni and then must supply another verb, not available in the context. This seems like too much machinery to me, since the p─Бda is readily interpretable on the syntactic pattern in c.

Griffith

Indra, thou humbledst tribes that spake with insult by breaking down seven autumn forts, their refuge.
Thou stirredst, Blameless! billowy floods, and gavest his foe a prey to youthful Purukutsa.

Geldner

Du, Indra, bezwangst die mitredenden St├дmme, als er ihre Zuflucht, die sieben herbstlichen Burgen brach. Du Makelloser setztest die flutenden Gew├дsser in Bewegung; du unterwarfst dem jugendlichen Purukutsa den Vritra.

Grassmann

Du, Indra, straftest da die Schm├дherst├дmme, als ihre Wehr du brachst, die sieben Burgen; Den Wasserstrom entliessest du, o reiner, gabst hin den Feind dem jungen Purukutsa.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGo the cities inhabited by the r─Бkс╣гasas, and thence to heaven (attended), receiver of many sacrifices by those who (attend you). Defend, like a lion, the untamed, quick-moving Agni, that he may abide in his dwelling, fulfilling his functions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To the cities inhabited by r─Бkс╣гasas: vс╣Ыtaс╕е ┼Ыura patn─лс╕е = raksobhiс╕е p─Бlayit─Б vс╣Ыtaс╕е pur─лс╕е; defend like a lion: as a lion protects the forest, in which his lair is, from the depredations of other animals

Jamison Brereton

Drive the troops whose lord is a champion [=you], Indra, and (those [=Maruts?]) with whom now (you gain?) heaven, much invoked one.
Guard insatiable Agni going in triumph; like a lion, (guard) his labors in the house at dawn.

Griffith

With whom thou drivest troops whose lords are heroes, and bringest daylight now, much worshipped Indra,
With them guard lion-like wasting active Agni to dwell in our tilled fields and in our homestead.

Geldner

F├╝hre die Heere zum Kampf, die in dir, Indra, einen tapferen Gebieter haben, und den Himmel, mit denen du jetzt, du Vielgerufener, verb├╝ndet bist. Hab acht auf Agni, auf Asusa, auf Turvayana! Wie ein L├╢we soll Agni, wie des Morgens im Hause, seine Werke verrichten.

Grassmann

Treib’, Indra, an der G├╢tterfrauen Scharen, den Himmel, Herr, mit den vereinten Helden, Bewahr das Feuer, das verzehrt und vordringt, dem L├╢wen gleich im Haus des Morgens Werke.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet (your foes, Indra), humbled by the might of your thunderbolt rest in their own station, for your glory; when you move, (armed) with your weapons, you send down the waters; arresting your horses, increase, by your power, (the abundance of) food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rest in their own station: in the firmament, the enemies are the clouds

Jamison Brereton

They [=enemies] will lie now in the same womb, Indra, for the
glorification of your metal-edged weapon in its greatness.
When by battle he sent the floods, the cows surging downward, he
mounted his two fallow bays; boldly he swiped the battle-prizes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes ab as a direct quote (uttered by unidentified speakers). He presumably does this because of the difference in tense/mood (subjunctive vs. injunctive) and person (2nd vs. 3rd) between ab and cd. But since such switches are common in the RV, the direct speech does not seem necessary or contextually supported.

Griffith

They through the greatness of thy spear, O Indra, shall, to thy praise, rest in this earthly station.
To loose the floods, to seek, for kine, the battle, his Bays he mounted boldly seized the booty.

Geldner

Die sollen nun im gleichen Scho├Яe liegen, o Indra, zu hohen Ehren der Pavirakeule." Als er durch Kampf die Gew├дsser, die K├╝he befreite, da bestieg er das Falbenpaar und strich mutig die Siegesgewinne ein.

Grassmann

Die Feinde lass im Schooss der Erde liegen, zum Ruhm, o Indra, durch die Macht des Blitzes; Lass Fluten str├╢men, wenn zum Kampf du eilest, besteig’ die Rosse, k├╝hn gewinne Beute.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдореН рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдорд╛рдирдореГрд╖рд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рд╕реНрдпреВрдордиреНрдпреВ ред тАШрд╕реНрдпреВрдордХрдореН’ (рдирд┐. рей. рем. рел) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦ- рдирд╛рдо ред рддрджрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреМ рд╕рддрддрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдиреМ рд╡рд╛ рдЛрдЬреНрд░рд╛ рдЛрдЬреБрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдиреМ рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╡реЗрдЧреМ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рддрджреАрдпрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡реМ рд╡рд╣ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдп ред рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд┐ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдВ рдЪрд╛рдХрди рдХрд╛рдордпрд╕реЗ рддрд░реНрдкрдпрд╕реЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдореН ред рддрджрд░реНрдердВ рд╕реВрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рдЪрдХреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдордгреНрдбрд▓рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдердЪрдХреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ рдЖрд╕рдиреНрдиреЗ рджреЗрд╢реЗ рдмреГрд╣рддрд╛рддреН рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдВ рдЧрдордпрддреБ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддреБ ред рдЕрде рдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд╣ред рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдГ рдЕрдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕реНрдкреГрдзрдГ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЕрднрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕рд┐рд╖рддреН рдЕрднрд┐рдпрд╛рддреБ рее рее резрем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBear, Indra, with your obedient horses, as swift as the wind, (the sage) Kutsa, to that ceremony (to which) you desire (to convey him); let the sun bring near the wheel of his chariot, and let the thunder-armed advance against his opponents.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Convey Kutsa, Indra, in whom you take pleasure. Eager for the halter are the two silvery horses of the Wind.
Then tear off the wheel of the Sun at the moment of encounter. Mace in hand, he will charge the opponents.

Jamison Brereton Notes

One of the few тАЬfuture imperativesтАЭ in the RV: vс╣Ыhat─Бt in c, following v├бha in p─Бda a. Geldner and Renou also supply an impv. in b (тАЬlenke,тАЭ тАЬatteleтАЭ), but this p─Бda makes a fine nominal clause (so also Hoffmann, Inj., 190).

Griffith

Indra, bear Kutsa, him in whom thou joyest: the dark-red horses of the Wind are docile.
Let the Sun roll his chariot wheel anear us, and let the Thunderer go to meet the foemen.

Geldner

Fahre den Kutsa, an dem du Wohlgefallen gefunden hast, o Indra, und lenke die Schimmelrosse des Vata, die dem Z├╝gel gehorchen! Rei├Я das Rad der Sonne dicht heranfahrend ab!" So trat er mit der Keule im Arm den Feinden entgegen.

Grassmann

Der dir gef├дllt, den Kutsa fahr, o Indra; am Z├╝gel ziehn des Windes rothe Rosse; Das Rad der Sonne treibe vor zum Schauen, den Blitz im Arme geh dem Feind entgegen.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕рд╛ рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдЬреАрддрдХрд░ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХреЛ рдмрдврд╝рд╛рд╡реЗ рее рел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд╣) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдп (рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдореН) рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕рднреЗрд╢ (рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рдЪрд╛рдХрдиреН) рдХрд╛рдордпрд╕реЗред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдХрдиреА рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдЧрддрд┐рд╖реНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рд▓реНрд▓рдЩреЛ рдордзреНрдпрдореИрдХрд╡рдЪрдиреЗ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрддрд┐ рд╢рдкрдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рд╢реНрд▓реБрдГ рд╢реНрд▓рд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрд╡рдВ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдЩреНрдпреЛрдЧреЗрдкреАрддреНрдпрдбрднрд╛рд╡рдГ, рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рдиреНрддрд╕рд▓реЛрдкрд╢реНрдЪред (рд╕реНрдпреВрдордиреНрдпреВ) рдЖрддреНрдордирдГ рд╕реНрдпреВрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдВ рдЧрдордирдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреВ (рдЛрдЬреНрд░рд╛) рдЛрдЬреБрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдиреМ (рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп) рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░рд┐рд╡ (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реМ (рдкреНрд░) (рд╕реВрд░рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ (рдЪрдХреНрд░рдореН) рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдореН (рд╡реГрд╣рддрд╛рддреН) рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзрдпрдиреНрддреБ (рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдЕрднрд┐) рд╕рдиреНрдореБрдЦреЗ (рд╕реНрдкреГрдзрдГ) рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН (рдпрд╛рд╕рд┐рд╖рддреН) рдпрд╛рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрддреБ (рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдГ) рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдГ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдореНрдмрд╛рд╣реНрд╡реЛрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рее рел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, lord of steeds, invigorated by our animating praise, you have slain those who make you no offerings and disturb your worshippers; but they who look upon you as (their) protector, and are associated for (the presentation of sacrificial) food, obtain from the posterity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Once you had smashed those who rout their allies, and had smashed the impious when you were strengthened by the stimulant, o Indra of the fallow bays,
those who saw before them Aryaman in company with these two [=Mitra and Varuс╣Зa], they were shattered by you, taking their progeny along.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. joins IndraтАЩs overwhelming aggressive power with the moral force of the three principal ─Аdityas. Those who offend against the strictures of the ─Аdityas get utterly destroyed by Indra, in a partnership that one might expect to be more prominent in the RV; X.89.9, adduced by Oldenberg, shows the same cooperative enterprise in clearer form.

I take the pf. part. jaghanv─Б╠Бn here as the equivalent of a pluperfect (in the English grammatical sense), a past anterior, since there are no finite forms with that function.

The standard tr. take both mitr├йru- and cod├б- as PNs. This is certainly the easy, and tempting, way out. But both can be (and in my opinion should be) given lexical weight. The easier one is cod├б-, a transparent derivative of тИЪcud тАШbestir, inciteтАЩ. GrassmannтАЩs interpr. of the compound (тЖР Roth), that cod├б- тАШinciting, goadingтАЩ is used of soma, makes good sense in context, since Indra performs his feats of strength under the influence of soma.

As for mitr├йru-, my interpr. is based on, but modifies, OldenbergтАЩs suggested mitr─Б─л╠Бru- тАЬdie Mitra (zur Rache ihrer Treulosigkeit) in Bewegung setzen.тАЭ He seems to envision the god Mitra being sent to punish the disloyal, but those who send Mitra to effect this punishment should be on the side of good, not subject to IndraтАЩs smiting as here. I take mitra- here as the common noun тАШallyтАЭ and the -─лr(u)- as expressing a hostile dispatching of their erstwhile allies. Both those who dishonor their alliances in this way and those who lack piety (├бd─Бs┼лn, b) violate the norms of ─Аrya society that are overseen by the ─Аdityas.

Although of the trio of principal ─Аdityas only Aryaman is named in this vs., Mitra lurks in the compound just discussed. Varuс╣Зa, unnamed, is present along with Mitra in the dual pronoun ay├│с╕е (in s├бc─Бy├│с╕е). Although the Pp reads ─Бy├│с╕е and Geldner accepts this reading (though see his n. 6c), I follow OldenbergтАЩs alternative analysis (so also Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) and his identification of the two as Mitra and Varuс╣Зa. I assume that тАЬsaw before them Aryaman with those twoтАЭ implies that the evil-doers have a vision of the three ─Аdityas sitting in judgment (vel sim.) before Indra destroys them.

┼Ы┼лrt├б- presumably belongs with ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бti, etc., though the vocalism is surprising; we would expect *┼Ы─лrta-, like AV ┼Ы─лс╣Ыс╣З├б-. [Add ref. to Clayton, when there is one.]

Griffith

Thou Indra, Lord of Bays, made strong by impulse, hast slain the vexers of thy friends, who give not.
They who beheld the Friend beside the living were cast aside by thee as they rode onward.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sage praises you, Indra, for the grant of desirable (food), since you have made the earth the bed of the asura; Maghavan has made the three (regions) marvellous by his gifts, and has destroyed for (the prince) Duryoс╣Зi (the asura), Kuyav─Бca, in combat.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The three regions: bh┼лmiс╕е is added to the term of the text, tisraс╕е: either earth in three aspects as identical with the three rituals of the dar┼Ыa or lunar periods; the pa┼Ыu or victim; and Soma, or libation; or, as implying earth, firmament and heaven

Jamison Brereton

The sage poet [=U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya?] murmured, o Indra, at the winning of the chants [/(sunтАЩs) rays]: тАЬHe has made the earth a pillow for
the D─Бsa.
The bounteous one will make the three (worlds?) bright with drops; he has embedded in a woeful womb the one who speaks evil in scorn.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As often in a mythological context, kav├н- by itself seems to refer to U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya. The previous mention (vs. 5) of Kutsa, often associated with UK, supports this assumption.

ark├бs─Бtau probably has a double sense. In the ritual context the ark├б- are the chants (see nearby I.176.5), but in the mythological context supplied by vs. 5 (esp. c), it can be the rays of the sun. So VI.26.3, which contains both UK and Kutsa.

тАЬMaking earth a pillowтАЭ is surely a euphemism for sending him to тАЬhis eternal rest,тАЭ тАЬputting him to sleepтАЭ among other such sayings. The тАЬwoeful wombтАЭ of d is a similar expression. Both remind us of 4a тАЬthey will now lie in the same womb,тАЭ clearly also referring to the grave.

Geldner tentatively takes the referent of fem. тАЬthreeтАЭ (tisr├бс╕е) as rivers, and he is followed by Renou and Witzel Got┼Н. Although this identification handles the gender and the fact that the adj. d─Б╠Бnucitra- (3x) is once used of waters (V.31.6), it runs into the problem that the canonical number of rivers is seven, not three. It is rather the divisions of the world/earth that are regularly triadic; cf. fem. tisr├бс╕е prthiv ╠е ─л╠Бс╕е (I.34.8), tisr├│ bh┼л╠Бm─лс╕е (II.27.8). Although тАЬbright with dropsтАЭ may not be the most natural way of referring to the three worlds, I think the numerology trumps the adjective – which could, in fact, mean тАШbright with giftsтАЩ, not тАШdropsтАЩ.

Geldner takes the loc. mс╣Ыdh├н as parallel to loc. duryoс╣З├й (тАЬin ein b├╢ses Nest, in MissachtungтАЭ), and as so often he is followed by Renou and Witzel Got┼Н; all of them also take k├║yav─Бcam as a PN. But given mс╣Ыdhr├бv─Бcaс╕е тАШof scornful speechтАЩ in 2a, it seems better to give k├║yav─Бc- lexical value and construe it with mс╣Ыdh├н.

Griffith

Indra, the bard sang forth in inspiration: thou madest earth a covering for the Dasa.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sages have celebrated your everlasting (as well as your) recent (exploits, in achieving which) you have endured many injuries in putting an end to war; verily, you have demolished hostile and undivine cities; you have bowed down the thunderbolt of the undivine asura.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These are your old (deeds), Indra; new ones have come: you
overpowered and exploded the many (strongholds) for the lack of joy [/end of battle] (of the godless).
You split the godless (clans) into pieces, like strongholds; you bowed the weapon of the godless reviler.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is much disagreement about the first hemistich because of the uncertain grammatical identity of several forms as well as a sandhi problem in p─Бda a and a hapax in b. Let us begin with the sandhi problem. The clear neut. pl. s├бn─Б t─Б╠Б тАЬthose old (things [=deeds?])тАЭ that opens the verse seems rhetorically paired with n├бvy─Б тАШnewтАЩ towards the end of the p─Бda, but in its sandhi situation, before vowelinitial ─Б╠Бguс╕е, n├бvy─Б should underlyingly end in -─Бс╕е, a masc. nom. pl. or fem. nom./acc. pl. (so Pp). Most standard tr. try to reflect this sandhi one way or another: Geldner takes the ref. to be n├бbhaс╕е in b, which he takes as a fem. pl. root noun n├бbh-. But тАЬThese are your old (deeds). New (clouds) have comeтАЭ is, with all due respect to Geldner, absurd.

Oldenberg takes both s├бhaс╕е and n├бbhaс╕е of b (with better semantics than тАШcloudsтАЩ – viz., тАЬneue Siege und BerstungenтАЭ) as the referent of n├бvy─Б(с╕е), though he does show some sympathy with GrassmannтАЩs suggestion that n├бvy─Б is the neut. pl. we want, in hiatus. Renou supplies тАЬhymnsтАЭ with n├бvy─Б(с╕е) тАж n├бbhaс╕е, which has no contextual support. Only Witzel Got┼Н, at least by implication, allow the neut. pl. interpr.: тАЬAlt sind diese deine (Heldentaten), o Indra. Neue sind (gerade) (hinzu)gekommen.тАЭ I think this is the only sensible way to interpret the passage: rhetorical patterning outweighs sandhi. The same hiatus of n├бvy─Б before a vowel is found in V.29.15 y─Б╠БтАж n├бvy─Б ├бkarma, where two vss. before (V.29.13) y─Б╠БтАж n├бvy─Б kс╣Ыс╣З├бvaс╕е essentially guarantees the neut. pl.

interpr.

The fem. pl. interpr. of n├бvy─Б(с╕е) is even less likely if s├бhaс╕е and/or n├бbhaс╕е are not taken as fem. pl. root nouns. As already noted, Oldenberg does so take them, and Geldner has the same analysis of n├бbhaс╕е, but not s├бhaс╕е, which he appears to take as a 2nd sg. verb in imperatival usage. Renou takes n├бbhaс╕е as a fem. pl. adj. and s├бhaс╕е as the neut. sg. of the s-stem; for Witzel Got┼Н s├бhaс╕е is a nom. pl. fem. to a root noun and n├бbhaс╕е a gen. sg., also to a root noun, dependent on ├бviraс╣З─Бya. The lack of agreement on basic grammatical identity almost reminds us of the interpretive chaos created by the Oldenberg Avestan G─Бthas. For my part I take both s├бhaс╕е and n├бbhaс╕е as 2nd sg. injunctives – s├бhas as the only act. finite form of the thematic stem s├бha- (though cf. part. s├бhant-), which is fairly well attested in the middle; n├бbhaс╕е as the act. transitive corresponding to med. intransitive 3rd pl. impv. n├бbhant─Бm тАЬlet them burst,тАЭ found esp. in the famous N─Бbh─Бka refrain (VIII.39-42). The fact that the next two p─Бdas (8c, 8d) open with 2nd sg. injunctives (bhin├бt and nan├бmaс╕е respectively) and that I.173 is characterized by p─Бda-initial 3rd sg. injunctives (see comm. above) supports the verbal interpr.

As for the rest of p─Бda b, I supply тАШstrongholdsтАЩ (p├║raс╕е) from p─Бda c with p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е, as in, e.g., I.63.2, II.14.6. The hapax ├бviraс╣Зa- I take as containing r├бс╣Зa- тАШjoyтАЩ / тАШbattleтАЩ, with both meanings in play in the cmpd. The form contains both the privative a- and what I consider a pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ v├н, both meaning тАШwithoutтАЩ. Although these elements might be expected to cancel each other out (тАЬnot without joy/battleтАЭ), I think the v├н is included to allow a buried pun on av─л╠Бra-, suggesting тАЬfor their unmanningтАЭ in addition to тАЬfor lack of joy / for non-battle [=end of battle].тАЭ The godless are supplied from the 2nd hemistich.

After the travails of ab, the rest of the verse is fairly straightforward. I supply v├н┼Ыaс╕е тАШclansтАЩ with ├бdev─лс╕е on the basis of the occurrence of this expression elsewhere (e.g., VI.49.15) and take bh├нdaс╕е (which, unlike the two -aс╕е forms in b, I do interpr as the acc. pl. of a root noun) as a kind of proleptic cognate acc. with bhin├бt: тАЬsplit тАж into smithereens.тАЭ I would in fact now substitute this more colorful expression for the published translation тАЬsplit into pieces.тАЭ

Griffith

These thine old deeds new bards have sung, O Indra. Thou conqueredst, boundest many tribes for ever.
Like castles thou hast crushed the godless races, and bowed the godless scorner’s deadly weapon.

Geldner

Dies sind deine alten Taten, Indra. Neue Wolken sind gekommen. ├Ьberwinde die vielen Wolken, da├Я die Unfreude aufh├╢re. Brich die gottlosen Einbr├╝che wie ihre Burgen; wende die Waffe des gottlosen Widersachers ab!

Grassmann

Dies alte, Indra, und dies neue r├╝hmt man: viel Frevler schlugst du, dass sie nimmer aufstehn, Zerbrachst wie Burgen die verruchten Rotten, des b├╢sen Schm├дhers Keule warfst du nieder.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, are the terrifier (of your foes); you have made the trembling waters overspread (the earth) like flowing rivers; but, hero, when you fill the ocean you have protected in their well-being Turva┼Ыa and Yadu.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like flowing rivers: s─лr─Бс╕е na sravant─лс╕е: s─лr─Б may be a certain river; or river, in genitive ral; you have protected:p─Бray─Б turva┼Ыam yadum svasti: p─Бraya = ap─Бlayaс╕е, you have protected;

Svasti = avin─Б┼Ыam, without loss or detriment;

P─Бraya = bear across, convey over in safety

Jamison Brereton

You, the tumultuous one, Indra, set the tumultuous waters in motion, flowing like streams.
When you will cross the sea, o champion, make Turva┼Ыa and Yadu
cross to well-being.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is identical to VI.20.12. This connection, in addition to the identical p─Бda I.174.2b=VI.20.10c establishes a relationship between the two hymns that makes the dependence of dart in our 2b on the one in VI.20.10c more likely.

The apparent -si impv. betrays its origins as an s-aor. subjunctive by appearing here in a subordinate clause, where impvs. are not licit.

Griffith

A Stormer thou hast made the stormy waters flow down, O Indra, like the running rivers.
When o’er the flood thou broughtest them, O Hero, thou keptest Turvasa and Yadu safely.

Du liessest brausend brausende Gew├дsser, o Indra, rinnen wie des Stromes Fluten, Wie du zum Meer, o Held, hindurch sie leitest, so f├╝hr zum Heile Turva├зa und Jadu.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBe you, Indra, at all times our especial defender; the preserver of our people, the bestower of strength upon all these our emulous (followers); that we may obtain food, strength, and long life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, should be at all times our man-protector of men, who best keeps the wolf away
and giver of victorious power over all our contenders. тАУ May we know refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Griffith

Indra, mayst thou be ours in all occasions, protector of the men, most gentle-hearted,
Giving us victory over all our rivals. May we find strengthening food in full abundance.

Geldner

Du, Indra, sollst uns allezeit der am meisten vor R├дubern sichernde Schirmer der M├дnner sein. Du gibst uns die ├Ьbermacht ├╝ber alle Gegner. - Wir m├╢chten einen gastfreien Opferb├╝ndler kennen lernen, der rasch schenkt.

Grassmann

Sei, Indra, unser du zu allen Zeiten, du als der M├дnner treuester Beschirmer, Du Sieg verleihend ├╝ber alle Feinde. Gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕реБрдЦ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдпрдо-рдирд┐рдпрдореЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдирд┐рдпрдд рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рдЪреМрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЫреЛрдбрд╝реЗ рд╣реБрдП рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдореЗрдВ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее резреж реердЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдХреГрддреНрдп рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдЪреМрд╣рддреНрддрд░рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕рддреНрд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рдкреВрд░рд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕реБрдЦрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рддрдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдз) рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реИрд╕реНрд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реИрд░рд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдзред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рдГред (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рднрд╡реЗрдГ (рдЕрд╡реГрдХрддрдордГ) рди рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡реГрдХрд╛рд╢реНрдЪреМрд░рд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреЗ рд╕реЛрд╜рддрд┐рд╢рдпрд┐рдд рдЗрддрд┐ (рдирд░рд╛рдореН) рдирд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН (рдиреГрдкрд╛рддрд╛) рдиреГрдгрд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ (рд╕рдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рдореН (рд╕реНрдкреГрдзрд╛рдореН) рдпреБрджреНрдзрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН (рд╕рд╣реЛрджрд╛рдГ) рдмрд▓рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдГ (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рдо (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрдВ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдореН (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рдЬреАрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдореН рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рдпрдорд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдирд┐рдпрддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрд╛рд╢реНрдЪреМрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорддреНрдпрдХреНрддрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╕реЗрд░рдБрд╕реНрддреЗ рдорд╣рджреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рее резреж реердЕрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реердЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд╕реНрд╕рдкреНрддрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдпрдо-рдирд┐рдпрдорд╛рдВрдиреА рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЗрдВрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рджрдорди рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реЗ рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рдЪреЛрд░реА рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░реВрди рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рдмрдиреВрди рдЖрдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдд рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд, рддреЗ рдЕрддреНрдпрдВрдд рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╢рд╛рд▓реА рдмрдирддрд╛рдд. рее резреж рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХреЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдпрд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рдЪреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрдд рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреА рдЬрд╛рдгрд▓реА рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее
